	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading mw-first-heading">GitHub</h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		<div id="contentSub2"></div>

		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Hosting service for software projects using Git</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Git" title="Git">Git</a> or <a href="/wiki/GitLab" title="GitLab">GitLab</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p><b>GitHub, Inc.</b> is a provider of <a href="/wiki/Internet_hosting_service" title="Internet hosting service">Internet hosting</a> for <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">software development</a> and <a href="/wiki/Version_control" title="Version control">version control</a> using <a href="/wiki/Git" title="Git">Git</a>. It offers the <a href="/wiki/Distributed_version_control" title="Distributed version control">distributed version control</a> and <a href="/wiki/Source_code_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Source code management">source code management</a> (SCM) functionality of Git, plus its own features. It provides <a href="/wiki/Access_control" title="Access control">access control</a> and several collaboration features such as <a href="/wiki/Bug_tracking_system" title="Bug tracking system">bug tracking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Software_feature" title="Software feature">feature</a> requests, <a href="/wiki/Task_management" title="Task management">task management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Continuous_integration" title="Continuous integration">continuous integration</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wiki" title="Wiki">wikis</a> for every project.<sup id="cite_ref-hugeinvestment_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hugeinvestment-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Headquartered in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, it has been a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> since 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-techcrunch_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techcrunch-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It is commonly used to host <a href="/wiki/Open-source" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source">open-source</a> projects.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> As of June 2022, GitHub reports having over 83&#160;million developers<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>  and more than 200&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Repository_(version_control)" title="Repository (version control)">repositories</a><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> (including at least 28&#160;million public repositories).<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> It is the largest <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a> host as of November&#160;2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GithubAWSTorontoSummit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/GithubAWSTorontoSummit.jpg/220px-GithubAWSTorontoSummit.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/GithubAWSTorontoSummit.jpg/330px-GithubAWSTorontoSummit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/GithubAWSTorontoSummit.jpg/440px-GithubAWSTorontoSummit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GithubAWSTorontoSummit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>GitHub at AWS Summit</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="GitHub.com">GitHub.com</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: GitHub.com">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Development of the GitHub.com platform began on October 19, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-beginning_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beginning-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-githuboneyear_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-githuboneyear-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-githubfirstcommit_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-githubfirstcommit-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The site was launched in April 2008 by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Preston-Werner" title="Tom Preston-Werner">Tom Preston-Werner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Wanstrath" title="Chris Wanstrath">Chris Wanstrath</a>, <a href="/wiki/P._J._Hyett" title="P. J. Hyett">P. J. Hyett</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Scott_Chacon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Scott Chacon (page does not exist)">Scott Chacon</a> after it had been made available for a few months prior as a beta release.<sup id="cite_ref-pastie_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pastie-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> GitHub has an annual <a href="/wiki/Keynote" title="Keynote">keynote</a> called GitHub Universe.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organizational_structure">Organizational structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Organizational structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>GitHub, Inc. was originally a <a href="/wiki/Flat_organization" title="Flat organization">flat organization</a> with no middle managers; in other words, "everyone is a manager" (<a href="/wiki/Workers%27_self-management" title="Workers&#39; self-management">self-management</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-cto-mgmt-style_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cto-mgmt-style-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Employees could choose to work on projects that interested them (<a href="/wiki/Open_allocation" title="Open allocation">open allocation</a>), but salaries were set by the chief executive.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (August 2014)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 2014, GitHub, Inc. introduced a layer of <a href="/wiki/Middle_management" title="Middle management">middle management</a> amid harassment claims made against senior management. <a href="/wiki/Tom_Preston-Werner" title="Tom Preston-Werner">Tom Preston-Werner</a> resigned as CEO amid the scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-2014_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-2014-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Finance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>GitHub.com was a <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship#Bootstrapping" title="Entrepreneurship">bootstrapped</a> <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">start-up business</a>, which in its first years provided enough revenue to be funded solely by its three founders and start taking on employees.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In July 2012, four years after the company was founded, <a href="/wiki/Andreessen_Horowitz" title="Andreessen Horowitz">Andreessen Horowitz</a> invested $100&#160;million in <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital" title="Venture capital">venture capital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hugeinvestment_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hugeinvestment-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In July 2015 GitHub raised another $250&#160;million of venture capital in a <a href="/wiki/Series_B" class="mw-redirect" title="Series B">series B round</a>. Investors were <a href="/wiki/Sequoia_Capital" title="Sequoia Capital">Sequoia Capital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andreessen_Horowitz" title="Andreessen Horowitz">Andreessen Horowitz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thrive_Capital" class="mw-redirect" title="Thrive Capital">Thrive Capital</a>, and other venture capital funds.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> As of 2018, GitHub was estimated to be generating $200–300&#160;million in Annual Recurring Revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-cnbc.com_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc.com-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
The GitHub service was developed by <a href="/wiki/Chris_Wanstrath" title="Chris Wanstrath">Chris Wanstrath</a>, <a href="/wiki/P._J._Hyett" title="P. J. Hyett">P. J. Hyett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Preston-Werner" title="Tom Preston-Werner">Tom Preston-Werner</a>, and Scott Chacon using <a href="/wiki/Ruby_on_Rails" title="Ruby on Rails">Ruby on Rails</a>, and started in February 2008. The company, GitHub, Inc., has existed since 2007 and is located in San Francisco.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mapping_collaborative_software_on_GitHub.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Mapping_collaborative_software_on_GitHub.png/220px-Mapping_collaborative_software_on_GitHub.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Mapping_collaborative_software_on_GitHub.png/330px-Mapping_collaborative_software_on_GitHub.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Mapping_collaborative_software_on_GitHub.png/440px-Mapping_collaborative_software_on_GitHub.png 2x" data-file-width="3508" data-file-height="1890" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mapping_collaborative_software_on_GitHub.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The shading of the map illustrates the number of users as a proportion of each country's <a href="/wiki/Internet_population" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet population">Internet population</a>. The circular charts surrounding the two hemispheres depict the total number of GitHub users (left) and commits (right) per country.</div></div></div>
<p>On February 24, 2009, GitHub announced that within the first year of being online, GitHub had accumulated over 46,000 public repositories, 17,000 of which were formed in the previous month. At that time, about 6,200 repositories had been <a href="/wiki/Fork_(software_development)" title="Fork (software development)">forked</a> at least once and 4,600 had been merged.
</p><p>That same year, the site was used by over 100,000 users, according to GitHub, and had grown to host 90,000 unique public repositories, 12,000 having been forked at least once, for a total of 135,000 repositories.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, GitHub was hosting 1 million repositories.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> A year later, this number doubled.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ReadWriteWeb" class="mw-redirect" title="ReadWriteWeb">ReadWriteWeb</a> reported that GitHub had surpassed <a href="/wiki/SourceForge" title="SourceForge">SourceForge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Google_Code" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Code">Google Code</a> in total number of commits for the period of January to May 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> On January 16, 2013, GitHub passed the 3 million users mark and was then hosting more than 5 million repositories.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the year, the number of repositories was twice as great, reaching 10 million repositories.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, GitHub raised $100 million in funding from <a href="/wiki/Andreessen_Horowitz" title="Andreessen Horowitz">Andreessen Horowitz</a> with a $750 million valuation.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>  On July 29, 2015, GitHub stated it had raised $250 million in funding in a round led by <a href="/wiki/Sequoia_Capital" title="Sequoia Capital">Sequoia Capital</a>. Other investors of that round included Andreessen Horowitz, Thrive Capital, and IVP (Institutional Venture Partners).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The round valued the company at approximately $2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, GitHub opened an office in Japan, its first outside of the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, GitHub was ranked No. 14 on the <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> Cloud 100 list.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> It was not featured on the 2018, 2019, and 2020 lists.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 28, 2018, GitHub fell victim to the third-largest <a href="/wiki/Distributed_denial-of-service" class="mw-redirect" title="Distributed denial-of-service">distributed denial-of-service</a> (DDoS) attack in history, with incoming traffic reaching a peak of about 1.35 terabits per second.<sup id="cite_ref-DDOS_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DDOS-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 19, 2018, GitHub expanded its GitHub Education by offering free education bundles to all schools.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisition_by_Microsoft">Acquisition by Microsoft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Acquisition by Microsoft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Number_of_open_source_contributors_by_company.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Number_of_open_source_contributors_by_company.png/220px-Number_of_open_source_contributors_by_company.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Number_of_open_source_contributors_by_company.png/330px-Number_of_open_source_contributors_by_company.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Number_of_open_source_contributors_by_company.png/440px-Number_of_open_source_contributors_by_company.png 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="795" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Number_of_open_source_contributors_by_company.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Microsoft on top of list of the ten organizations with the most open-source contributors on GitHub in 2016<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>From 2012, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> became a significant user of GitHub, using it to host open-source projects and development tools such as <a href="/wiki/.NET" title=".NET">.NET Core</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chakra_(JavaScript_engine)" title="Chakra (JavaScript engine)">Chakra Core</a>, <a href="/wiki/MSBuild" title="MSBuild">MSBuild</a>, <a href="/wiki/PowerShell" title="PowerShell">PowerShell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_PowerToys" title="Microsoft PowerToys">PowerToys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visual_Studio_Code" title="Visual Studio Code">Visual Studio Code</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows_Calculator" title="Windows Calculator">Windows Calculator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows_Terminal" title="Windows Terminal">Windows Terminal</a> and the bulk of its product documentation (now to be found on <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Docs" title="Microsoft Docs">Microsoft Docs</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-venturebeat_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-venturebeat-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 4, 2018, Microsoft announced its intent to acquire GitHub for US$7.5 billion. The deal closed on October 26, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> GitHub continued to operate independently as a community, platform and business.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Under Microsoft, the service was led by <a href="/wiki/Xamarin" title="Xamarin">Xamarin</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Nat_Friedman" title="Nat Friedman">Nat Friedman</a>, reporting to <a href="/wiki/Scott_Guthrie" title="Scott Guthrie">Scott Guthrie</a>, executive vice president of Microsoft Cloud and AI. GitHub's CEO, Chris Wanstrath, was retained as a "technical fellow," also reporting to Guthrie. Nat Friedman resigned November 3, 2021; replaced by Thomas Domke. <sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There have been concerns from developers Kyle Simpson, <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a> trainer and author, and Rafael Laguna, CEO at <a href="/wiki/Open-Xchange" title="Open-Xchange">Open-Xchange</a> over Microsoft's purchase, citing uneasiness over Microsoft's handling of previous acquisitions, such as <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Mobile" title="Microsoft Mobile">Nokia's mobile business</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This acquisition was in line with Microsoft's business strategy under CEO <a href="/wiki/Satya_Nadella" title="Satya Nadella">Satya Nadella</a>, which has seen a larger focus on <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a> services, alongside the development of and contributions to open-source software.<sup id="cite_ref-techcrunch_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techcrunch-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Harvard_Business_Review" title="Harvard Business Review">Harvard Business Review</a></i> argued that Microsoft was intending to acquire GitHub to get access to its user base, so it can be used as a <a href="/wiki/Loss_leader" title="Loss leader">loss leader</a> to encourage the use of its other development products and services.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Concerns over the sale bolstered interest in competitors: <a href="/wiki/Bitbucket" title="Bitbucket">Bitbucket</a> (owned by <a href="/wiki/Atlassian" title="Atlassian">Atlassian</a>), <a href="/wiki/GitLab" title="GitLab">GitLab</a> and <a href="/wiki/SourceForge" title="SourceForge">SourceForge</a> (owned by BIZX, LLC) reported that they had seen spikes in new users intending to migrate projects from GitHub to their respective services.<sup id="cite_ref-atlassian-10reasons_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atlassian-10reasons-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-zdnet-rivalsgain_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zdnet-rivalsgain-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2019, GitHub acquired Semmle, a code analysis tool.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In February 2020, GitHub launched in India under the name GitHub India Private Limited.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In March 2020, GitHub announced that they were acquiring <a href="/wiki/Npm_(software)" title="Npm (software)">npm</a>, a JavaScript packaging vendor, for an undisclosed sum of money.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The deal was closed on 15 April 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early July 2020, the GitHub Archive Program was established, to archive its open-source code in perpetuity.<sup id="cite_ref-blog_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blog-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>GitHub's <a href="/wiki/Mascot" title="Mascot">mascot</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphized" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthropomorphized">anthropomorphized</a> "octocat" with five <a href="/wiki/Cephalopod_limb" title="Cephalopod limb">octopus-like arms</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Octodex_FAQ_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Octodex_FAQ-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jaramillo_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jaramillo-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The character was created by graphic designer <a href="/wiki/Simon_Oxley" title="Simon Oxley">Simon Oxley</a> as <a href="/wiki/Clip_art" title="Clip art">clip art</a> to sell on <a href="/wiki/IStock" title="IStock">iStock</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-DeAmicis_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeAmicis-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> a website that enables designers to market <a href="/wiki/Royalty-free" title="Royalty-free">royalty-free</a> <a href="/wiki/Digital_image" title="Digital image">digital images</a>. GitHub became interested in Oxley's work after Twitter selected a bird that he designed for their own logo.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The illustration GitHub chose was a character that Oxley had named Octopuss.<sup id="cite_ref-DeAmicis_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeAmicis-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Since GitHub wanted Octopuss for their logo (a use that the iStock license disallows), they negotiated with Oxley to buy exclusive rights to the image.<sup id="cite_ref-DeAmicis_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeAmicis-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>GitHub renamed Octopuss to Octocat,<sup id="cite_ref-DeAmicis_58-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeAmicis-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and trademarked the character along with the new name.<sup id="cite_ref-Octodex_FAQ_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Octodex_FAQ-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Later, GitHub hired illustrator Cameron McEfee to adapt Octocat for different purposes on the website and promotional materials; McEfee and various GitHub users have since created hundreds of variations of the character, which are available on <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://octodex.github.com/">The Octodex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-McEfee_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McEfee-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Projects on GitHub.com can be accessed and managed using the standard <a href="/wiki/Git" title="Git">Git</a> command-line interface; all standard Git commands work with it. GitHub.com also allows users to browse public repositories on the site. Multiple desktop clients and Git <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_(computing)" title="Plug-in (computing)">plugins</a> are also available. The site provides <a href="/wiki/Social_networking" class="mw-redirect" title="Social networking">social networking</a>-like functions such as feeds, followers, wikis (using <a href="/wiki/Wiki_software" title="Wiki software">wiki software</a> called <a href="/wiki/Gollum_Wiki" class="mw-redirect" title="Gollum Wiki">Gollum</a>) and a <a href="/wiki/Collaboration_graph" title="Collaboration graph">social network graph</a> to display how developers work on their versions ("<a href="/wiki/Fork_(software_development)" title="Fork (software development)">forks</a>") of a repository and what fork (and branch within that fork) is newest.
</p><p>Anyone can browse and download public repositories but only registered users can contribute content to repositories. With a registered user account, users are able to have discussions, manage repositories, submit contributions to others' repositories, and <a href="/wiki/Code_review" title="Code review">review changes to code</a>. GitHub.com began offering limited private repositories at no cost in January 2019 (limited to three contributors per project). Previously, only public repositories were free.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:3_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> On April 14, 2020, GitHub made "all of the core GitHub features" free for everyone, including "private repositories with unlimited collaborators."<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The fundamental software that underpins GitHub is <a href="/wiki/Git" title="Git">Git</a> itself, written by <a href="/wiki/Linus_Torvalds" title="Linus Torvalds">Linus Torvalds</a>, creator of Linux.  The additional software that provides the GitHub user interface was written using <a href="/wiki/Ruby_on_Rails" title="Ruby on Rails">Ruby on Rails</a> and <a href="/wiki/Erlang_(programming_language)" title="Erlang (programming language)">Erlang</a> by GitHub, Inc. developers Wanstrath,<sup id="cite_ref-wanstrathinterview_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wanstrathinterview-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Hyett, and Preston-Werner.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scope">Scope</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Scope">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The main purpose of GitHub.com is to facilitate the <a href="/wiki/Version_control" title="Version control">version control</a> and <a href="/wiki/Issue_tracking_system" title="Issue tracking system">issue tracking</a> aspects of software development. Labels, milestones, responsibility assignment, and a search engine are available for issue tracking. For version control, Git (and by extension GitHub.com) allows <a href="/wiki/Pull_request" class="mw-redirect" title="Pull request">pull requests</a> to propose changes to the source code. Users with the ability to review the proposed changes can see a diff of the requested changes and approve them. In Git terminology, this action is called "committing" and one instance of it is a "commit." A history of all commits is kept and can be viewed at a later time.
</p><p>In addition, GitHub supports the following formats and features:
</p>
<ul><li>Documentation,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> including automatically rendered <a href="/wiki/README" title="README">README</a> files in a variety of <a href="/wiki/Markdown" title="Markdown">Markdown</a>-like file formats (see <a href="/wiki/README#On_GitHub" title="README">README §&#160;On GitHub</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wikis" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikis">Wikis</a><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>GitHub Actions,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> which allows building <a href="/wiki/Continuous_integration" title="Continuous integration">continuous integration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Continuous_deployment" title="Continuous deployment">continuous deployment</a> pipelines for testing, releasing and deploying software without the use of third-party websites/platforms</li>
<li>Graphs: pulse, contributors, commits, code frequency, punch card, network, members</li>
<li>Integrations Directory<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Email notifications<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Discussions<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Option to subscribe someone to notifications by <a href="/wiki/Mention_(blogging)" title="Mention (blogging)">@ mentioning</a> them.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emoji" title="Emoji">Emojis</a><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Nested <a href="/wiki/To_do_list" class="mw-redirect" title="To do list">task-lists</a> within files</li>
<li>Visualization of <a href="/wiki/Geospatial_analysis" class="mw-redirect" title="Geospatial analysis">geospatial</a> data</li>
<li>3D render files that can be previewed using a new integrated STL file viewer that displays the files on a "3D canvas."<sup id="cite_ref-3d_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3d-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The viewer is powered by <a href="/wiki/WebGL" title="WebGL">WebGL</a> and <a href="/wiki/Three.js" title="Three.js">Three.js</a>.</li>
<li>Photoshop's native PSD format can be previewed and compared to previous versions of the same file.</li>
<li>PDF document viewer</li>
<li>Security Alerts of known <a href="/wiki/Common_Vulnerabilities_and_Exposures" title="Common Vulnerabilities and Exposures">Common Vulnerabilities and Exposures</a> in different packages</li></ul>
<p>GitHub's Terms of Service do not require public software projects hosted on GitHub to meet the <a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Definition" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Source Definition">Open Source Definition</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Terms_of_service" title="Terms of service">terms of service</a> state, "By setting your repositories to be viewed publicly, you agree to allow others to view and fork your repositories."<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="GitHub_Enterprise">GitHub Enterprise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: GitHub Enterprise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>GitHub Enterprise is a self-managed version of GitHub.com with similar functionality. It can be run on an organization's own hardware or on a cloud provider, and it has been available since November 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In November 2020, source code for GitHub Enterprise Server was leaked online in an apparent protest against DMCA takedown of <a href="/wiki/Youtube-dl" title="Youtube-dl">youtube-dl</a>. According to GitHub, the source code came from GitHub accidentally sharing the code with Enterprise customers themselves, not from an attack on GitHub servers.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="GitHub_Pages">GitHub Pages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: GitHub Pages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>GitHub Pages</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Static_web_page" title="Static web page">static</a> <a href="/wiki/Web_hosting_service" title="Web hosting service">web hosting service</a> offered by GitHub since 2008 to GitHub users for hosting user <a href="/wiki/Blog" title="Blog">blogs</a>, project documentation,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> or even whole books created as a page.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>All GitHub Pages content is stored in a Git repository, either as files served to visitors verbatim or in <a href="/wiki/GitHub_Flavored_Markdown" class="mw-redirect" title="GitHub Flavored Markdown">Markdown</a> format. GitHub is seamlessly integrated with <a href="/wiki/Jekyll_(software)" title="Jekyll (software)">Jekyll</a> static website and blog generator and GitHub continuous integration pipelines. Each time the content source is updated, Jekyll regenerates the website and automatically serves it via GitHub Pages infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As with the rest of GitHub, it includes both free and paid tiers of service, instead of being supported by <a href="/wiki/Online_advertising" title="Online advertising">web advertising</a>. Websites generated through this service are hosted either as <a href="/wiki/Subdomain" title="Subdomain">subdomains</a> of the github.io domain, or as custom <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domains</a> bought through a third-party <a href="/wiki/Domain_name_registrar" title="Domain name registrar">domain name registrar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>  When a custom domain is set on a GitHub Pages repo a <a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Encrypt" title="Let&#39;s Encrypt">Let's Encrypt</a> certificate for it is generated automatically.  Once the certificate has been generated Enforce HTTPS can be set for the repository's website to transparently redirect all HTTP requests to HTTPS.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gist">Gist</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Gist">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>GitHub also operates a <a href="/wiki/Pastebin" title="Pastebin">pastebin</a>-style site called <b>Gist</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-pastie_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pastie-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> which is for <a href="/wiki/Snippet_(programming)" title="Snippet (programming)">code snippets</a>, as opposed to GitHub proper, which is for larger projects.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Tom Preston-Werner débuted the feature at a Ruby conference in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gist builds on the traditional simple concept of a <a href="/wiki/Pastebin" title="Pastebin">pastebin</a> by adding version control for code snippets, easy forking, and <a href="/wiki/Transport_Layer_Security" title="Transport Layer Security">TLS encryption</a> for private pastes. Because each "gist" is its own Git repository, multiple code snippets can be contained in a single page and they can be pushed and pulled using Git.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Unregistered users were able to upload Gists until March 19, 2018, when uploading gists was restricted to logged-in users, reportedly to mitigate <a href="/wiki/Spamming" title="Spamming">spamming</a> on the page of recent gists.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gists' <a href="/wiki/URL" title="URL">URLs</a> use hexadecimal IDs, and edits to gists are recorded in a <a href="/wiki/Version_control" title="Version control">revision history</a>, which can show the text difference of thirty revisions per page with an option between a "split" and "unified" view. Like repositories, Gists can be forked, "starred", i.e. publicly bookmarked, and commented on. The count of revisions, stars, and forks is indicated on the gist page.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_program">Education program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Education program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>GitHub launched a new program called the GitHub Student Developer Pack to give students free access to popular development tools and services. GitHub partnered with <a href="/wiki/Bitnami" title="Bitnami">Bitnami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crowdflower" class="mw-redirect" title="Crowdflower">Crowdflower</a>, <a href="/wiki/DigitalOcean" title="DigitalOcean">DigitalOcean</a>, <a href="/wiki/DNSimple" title="DNSimple">DNSimple</a>, <a href="/wiki/HackHands" title="HackHands">HackHands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Namecheap" title="Namecheap">Namecheap</a>, Orchestrate, Screenhero, <a href="/wiki/SendGrid" title="SendGrid">SendGrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stripe_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stripe (company)">Stripe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Travis_CI" title="Travis CI">Travis CI</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Unreal_Engine" title="Unreal Engine">Unreal Engine</a> to launch the program.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016 GitHub announced the launch of the GitHub Campus Experts program<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> to train and encourage students to grow technology communities at their universities. The Campus Experts program is open to university students 18 years and older across the world.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> GitHub Campus Experts are one of the primary ways that GitHub funds student-oriented events and communities, Campus Experts are given access to training, funding, and additional resources to run events and grow their communities. To become a Campus Expert applicants must complete an online training course consisting of multiple modules designed to grow community leadership skills.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="GitHub_Marketplace_service">GitHub Marketplace service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: GitHub Marketplace service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>GitHub also provides some <a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_service" title="Software as a service">software as a service</a> ("SaaS") integrations for adding extra features to projects. Those services include:
</p>
<ul><li>Waffle.io: Project management for software teams. Automatically see pull requests, automated builds, reviews, and deployments across all of your repositories in GitHub.</li>
<li>Rollbar: Integrate with GitHub to provide real-time debugging tools and full-stack exception reporting. It is compatible with all popular code languages, such as <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>, <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a>, <a href="/wiki/.NET_Framework" title=".NET Framework">.NET</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruby_(programming_language)" title="Ruby (programming language)">Ruby</a>, <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Node.js" title="Node.js">Node.js</a>, <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>, <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Go_(programming_language)" title="Go (programming language)">Go</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>, and <a href="/wiki/C_Sharp_(programming_language)" title="C Sharp (programming language)">C#</a>.</li>
<li>Codebeat: For automated code analysis specialized in web and mobile developers. The supported languages for this software are <a href="/wiki/Elixir_(programming_language)" title="Elixir (programming language)">Elixir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Go_(programming_language)" title="Go (programming language)">Go</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swift_(programming_language)" title="Swift (programming language)">Swift</a>, <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>, <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruby_(programming_language)" title="Ruby (programming language)">Ruby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kotlin_(programming_language)" title="Kotlin (programming language)">Kotlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Objective-C" title="Objective-C">Objective-C</a>, and <a href="/wiki/TypeScript" title="TypeScript">TypeScript</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Travis_CI" title="Travis CI">Travis CI</a>: To provide confidence for your apps while doing test and ship. Also gives full control over the build environment, to adapt it to the code. Supported languages: <a href="/wiki/Go_(programming_language)" title="Go (programming language)">Go</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>, <a href="/wiki/Objective-C" title="Objective-C">Objective-C</a>, <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a>, <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruby_(programming_language)" title="Ruby (programming language)">Ruby</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swift_(programming_language)" title="Swift (programming language)">Swift</a>.</li>
<li>GitLocalize: Developed for teams that are translating their content from one point to another. GitLocalize automatically syncs with your repository so you can keep your workflow on GitHub. It also keeps you updated on what needs to be translated.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="GitHub_Sponsors">GitHub Sponsors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: GitHub Sponsors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>GitHub Sponsors allows users to make monthly money donations to projects hosted on GitHub.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The public beta was announced on May 23, 2019, and the project accepts waitlist registrations. <a href="/wiki/The_Verge" title="The Verge">The Verge</a> said that GitHub Sponsors "works exactly like <a href="/wiki/Patreon" title="Patreon">Patreon</a>" because "developers can offer various funding tiers that come with different perks, and they'll receive recurring payments from supporters who want to access them and encourage their work" except with "zero fees to use the program." Furthermore, GitHub offers incentives for early adopters during the first year: it pledges to cover payment processing costs and match sponsorship payments up to $5,000 per developer. Furthermore, users still can use other similar services like Patreon and Open Collective and link to their own websites.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="GitHub_Archive_Program">GitHub Archive Program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: GitHub Archive Program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In July 2020, GitHub stored a February archive of the site<sup id="cite_ref-blog_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blog-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> in an abandoned mountain mine in <a href="/wiki/Svalbard" title="Svalbard">Svalbard</a>, Norway, part of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_World_Archive" title="Arctic World Archive">Arctic World Archive</a> and not far from the <a href="/wiki/Svalbard_Global_Seed_Vault" title="Svalbard Global Seed Vault">Svalbard Global Seed Vault</a>. The archive contained the code of all active public repositories, as well as that of dormant, but significant public repositories. The 21<a href="/wiki/Terabyte" class="mw-redirect" title="Terabyte">TB</a> of data was stored on <a href="/w/index.php?title=PiqlFilm&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="PiqlFilm (page does not exist)">piqlFilm</a> archival film reels as <a href="/wiki/Barcode#Matrix_(2D)_barcodes" title="Barcode">matrix (2D) barcode</a> (<a href="/wiki/Boxing_barcode" title="Boxing barcode">Boxing barcode</a>), and is expected to last 500–1,000 years.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-buried_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buried-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The GitHub Archive Program is also working with partners on Project Silica, in an attempt to store all public repositories for 10,000 years. It aims to write archives into the molecular structure of <a href="/wiki/Quartz_glass" class="mw-redirect" title="Quartz glass">quartz glass</a> platters, using a  high-precision laser that pulses a <a href="/wiki/Quadrillion" class="mw-redirect" title="Quadrillion">quadrillion</a> (1,000,000,000,000,000) times per second.<sup id="cite_ref-buried_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buried-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Criticism_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-criticism" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" decoding="async" width="45" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="354" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article's <i>Criticism</i> or <i>Controversy</i> section <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view#Article_structure" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">may compromise the article's neutrality</a></b> by separating out potentially negative information.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please integrate the section's contents into the article as a whole, or rewrite the material.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2021</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Harassment_allegations">Harassment allegations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Harassment allegations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 2014, GitHub programmer <a href="/w/index.php?title=Julie_Ann_Horvath&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Julie Ann Horvath (page does not exist)">Julie Ann Horvath</a> alleged that founder and CEO Tom Preston-Werner and his wife, Theresa, engaged in a pattern of harassment against her that led to her leaving the company.<sup id="cite_ref-Valleywag_March_2014_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Valleywag_March_2014-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> In April 2014, GitHub released a statement denying Horvath's allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTResigns_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTResigns-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> However, following an internal investigation, GitHub confirmed the claims. GitHub's CEO Chris Wanstrath wrote on the company blog, "The investigation found Tom Preston-Werner in his capacity as GitHub's CEO acted inappropriately, including confrontational conduct, disregard of workplace complaints, insensitivity to the impact of his spouse's presence in the workplace, and failure to enforce an agreement that his spouse should not work in the office."<sup id="cite_ref-Follow_up_to_the_investigation_results_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Follow_up_to_the_investigation_results-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Preston-Werner subsequently resigned from the company.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The firm then announced it would implement new initiatives and trainings  "to make sure employee concerns and conflicts are taken seriously and dealt with appropriately."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sanctions">Sanctions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sanctions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On July 25, 2019, a developer based in Iran wrote on <a href="/wiki/Medium_(website)" title="Medium (website)">Medium</a> that GitHub had blocked his private repositories  and prohibited access to GitHub pages.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Soon after, GitHub confirmed that it was now blocking developers in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> from accessing private repositories.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> However, GitHub reopened access to GitHub Pages days later, for public repositories regardless of location. It was also revealed that using GitHub while visiting sanctioned countries could result in similar actions occurring on a user's account. GitHub responded to complaints and the media through a spokesperson, saying:
</p>
<blockquote><p>GitHub is subject to US trade control laws, and is committed to full compliance with applicable law. At the same time, GitHub's vision is to be the global platform for <a href="/wiki/Developer_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Developer (software)">developer</a> collaboration, no matter where developers reside. As a result, we take seriously our responsibility to examine government mandates thoroughly to be certain that users and customers are not impacted beyond what is required by law. This includes keeping public repositories services, including those for open source projects, available and accessible to support personal communications involving developers in sanctioned regions.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Developers who feel that they should not have restrictions can appeal for the removal of said restrictions, including those who only travel to, and do not reside in, those countries. GitHub has forbidden the use of <a href="/wiki/Virtual_private_network" title="Virtual private network">VPNs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Proxy_server" title="Proxy server">IP proxies</a> to access the site from sanctioned countries, as purchase history and IP addresses are how they flag users, among other sources.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Censorship">Censorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Censorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Censorship_of_GitHub" title="Censorship of GitHub">Censorship of GitHub</a></div><p>On December 3, 2014, Russia blacklisted GitHub.com because GitHub initially refused to take down user-posted suicide manuals.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> After a day, Russia withdrew its block,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> and GitHub began blocking specific content and pages in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> On December 31, 2014, India blocked GitHub.com along with 31 other websites over pro-<a href="/wiki/ISIS" class="mw-redirect" title="ISIS">ISIS</a> content posted by users;<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> the block was lifted three days later.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> On October 8, 2016, Turkey blocked GitHub to prevent email leakage of a hacked account belonging to the country's energy minister.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 26, 2015, a large-scale <a href="/wiki/DDoS" class="mw-redirect" title="DDoS">DDoS</a> attack was launched against GitHub.com that lasted for just under five days.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The attack, which appeared to originate from China, primarily targeted GitHub-hosted user content describing methods of <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_circumvention" title="Internet censorship circumvention">circumventing Internet censorship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 19, 2020, Chinese police detained Chen Mei and Cai Wei (volunteers for Terminus 2049, a project hosted on GitHub), and accused them of "picking quarrels and provoking trouble." Cai and Chen archived news articles, interviews, and other materials published on Chinese media outlets, and social media platforms that have been removed by censors in China.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ICE_contract">ICE contract</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: ICE contract">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>GitHub has a $200,000 contract with <a href="/wiki/U.S._Immigration_and_Customs_Enforcement" title="U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement">U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement</a> (ICE) for the use of their on-site product GitHub Enterprise Server. This contract was renewed in 2019, despite internal opposition from many GitHub employees. In an email sent to employees, later posted to the GitHub blog on October 9, 2019, CEO <a href="/wiki/Nat_Friedman" title="Nat Friedman">Nat Friedman</a> stated "The revenue from the purchase is less than $200,000 and not financially material for our company." He announced that GitHub had pledged to donate $500,000 to "nonprofit groups supporting immigrant communities targeted by the current administration."<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> In response, at least 150 GitHub employees signed an open letter re-stating their opposition to the contract, and denouncing alleged human rights abuses by ICE. As of November 13, 2019, five workers had resigned over the contract.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The ICE contract dispute came into focus again in June 2020 due to the company's decision <a href="/wiki/Master/slave_(technology)#Terminology_concerns" title="Master/slave (technology)">to abandon "master/slave" branch terminology</a>, spurred by the George Floyd protests and <a href="/wiki/Black_Lives_Matter" title="Black Lives Matter">Black Lives Matter</a> movement.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Detractors of GitHub describe the branch renaming to be a form of <a href="/wiki/Performative_activism" title="Performative activism">performative activism</a> and have urged GitHub to cancel their ICE contract instead.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> An open letter from members of the open source community was shared on GitHub in December 2019, demanding that the company drop its contract with ICE and provide more transparency into how they conduct business and partnerships. The letter has been signed by more than 700 people.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capitol_riot_comments_and_employee_firing">Capitol riot comments and employee firing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Capitol riot comments and employee firing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2021, GitHub fired one of its employees after he expressed concern for colleagues as a violent mob <a href="/wiki/2021_storming_of_the_United_States_Capitol" class="mw-redirect" title="2021 storming of the United States Capitol">stormed the U.S. Capitol</a>, calling some of the rioters "Nazis."<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> After an investigation, GitHub's COO said there were "significant errors of judgment and procedure" with the company's decision to fire the employee. As a result of the investigation, GitHub reached out to the employee, and the company's head of human resources resigned.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Linus_Torvalds" title="Linus Torvalds">Linus Torvalds</a>, the original developer of the Git software, has criticized the merging ability of the GitHub interface.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Developed_projects">Developed projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=GitHub&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Developed projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Atom_(text_editor)" title="Atom (text editor)">Atom</a>, a free and open-source text and source code editor</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Electron_(software_framework)" title="Electron (software framework)">Electron</a>, an open-source framework to use JavaScript-based websites as desktop applications.</li></ul>
